## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|

| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Roslyn C# Type Inference and Overload Resolution Chain

## Your Task

Trace the type inference and method overload resolution pipeline in dotnet/roslyn. Find all C# source files under src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/ that participate in overload resolution. Identify: the OverloadResolution class and its main Resolve methods, the MethodTypeInferrer that performs generic type argument inference, the BetterFunctionMember comparison, the Conversions class used to rank implicit conversions, and the BestTypeInferrer for array/conditional expressions. Report each file path and key class.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/roslyn--v4.12.0.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

When a\\n23: particular method group is specified in a method invocation, and no type arguments\\n24: are specified as part of the method invocation, type inference is applied to each\\n25: generic method in the method group. If type inference succeeds, then the inferred\\n26: type arguments are used to determine the types of formal parameters for subsequent \\n27: overload resolution. If overload resolution chooses a generic method as the one to\\n28: invoke then the inferred type arguments are used as the actual type arguments for the\\n29: invocation. If type inference for a particular method fails, that method does not\\n30: participate in overload resolution. The failure of type inference, in and of itself,\\n31: does not cause a compile-time error. However, it often leads to a compile-time error\\n32: when overload resolution then fails to find any applicable methods.\\n33: \\n34: If the supplied number of arguments is different than the number of parameters in\\n35: the method, then inference immediately fails. Otherwise, assume that the generic\\n36: method has the following signature:\\n37: \\n38: Tr M<X1...Xn>(T1 x1 ... Tm xm)\\n39: \\n40: With a method call of the form M(E1...Em) the task of type inference is to find\\n41: unique type arguments S1...Sn for each of the type parameters X1...Xn so that the\\n42: call M<S1...Sn>(E1...Em)becomes valid.\\n43: \\n44: During the process of inference each type parameter Xi is either fixed to a particular\\n45: type Si or unfixed with an associated set of bounds. Each of the bounds is some type T.\\n46: Each bound is classified as an upper bound, lower bound or exact bound.\\n47: Initially each type variable Xi is unfixed with an empty set of bounds.\\n48: \\n49: */\\n50: \\n51: // This file contains the implementation for method type inference on calls (with\\n52: // arguments, and method type inference on conversion of method groups to delegate\\n53: When a\n23: particular method group is specified in a method invocation, and no type arguments\n24: are specified as part of the method invocation, type inference is applied to each\n25: generic method in the method group. If type inference succeeds, then the inferred\n26: type arguments are used to determine the types of formal parameters for subsequent \n27: overload resolution. If overload resolution chooses a generic method as the one to\n28: invoke then the inferred type arguments are used as the actual type arguments for the\n29: invocation. If type inference for a particular method fails, that method does not\n30: participate in overload resolution. The failure of type inference, in and of itself,\n31: does not cause a compile-time error. However, it often leads to a compile-time error\n32: when overload resolution then fails to find any applicable methods.\n33: \n34: If the supplied number of arguments is different than the number of parameters in\n35: the method, then inference immediately fails. Otherwise, assume that the generic\n36: method has the following signature:\n37: \n38: Tr M<X1...Xn>(T1 x1 ... Tm xm)\n39: \n40: With a method call of the form M(E1...Em) the task of type inference is to find\n41: unique type arguments S1...Sn for each of the type parameters X1...Xn so that the\n42: call M<S1...Sn>(E1...Em)becomes valid.\n43: \n44: During the process of inference each type parameter Xi is either fixed to a particular\n45: type Si or unfixed with an associated set of bounds. Supporting Data Structures\\n- **AnalyzedArguments** (AnalyzedArguments.cs): Pools analyzed argument expressions, names, and ref kinds\\n- **MemberResolutionResult<TMember>** (MemberResolutionResult.cs): Contains resolution outcome for individual members\\n- **MemberAnalysisResult** (MemberAnalysisResult.cs): Stores conversion sequences, constraint diagnostics, and argument-to-parameter mappings\\n- **OverloadResolution_ArgsToParameters.cs**: Handles complex argument-to-parameter mapping when named arguments, optional parameters, or params modifiers are involved\\n\\n## The Resolution Chain\\n\\n1. **MethodInvocationOverloadResolution** receives method candidates, type arguments, receiver, and arguments\\n2. For each candidate, **MethodTypeInferrer.Infer** is called to infer missing type arguments\\n3. Candidates are filtered by applicability (arguments match parameters)\\n4. **BetterFunctionMember** is called repeatedly to find the unique best member\\n5. For each parameter position, **Conversions.ClassifyImplicitConversionFromExpression** ranks the conversion quality\\n6. If needed, **BestTypeInferrer** infers target types for array/conditional expressions\\n7. The winning member is returned in the **OverloadResolutionResult<TMember>**\\n\\nThis pipeline implements the complete C# 7.x method invocation binding specification, handling generic type inference, overload resolution, and conversion ranking in a coordinated manner.\"\n}\nEOF\ncat /workspace/answer.json\n"

  "text": "The C# type inference and method overload resolution pipeline in Roslyn is implemented across multiple coordinated components in the src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/Semantics/ directory structure.\n\n## Pipeline Overview\n\nThe pipeline consists of several stages:\n\n### 1. Overload Resolution Entry Points (OverloadResolution.cs)\nThe OverloadResolution class provides three main public entry points:\n- **ObjectCreationOverloadResolution**: Resolves constructor candidates (line 101)\n- **MethodInvocationOverloadResolution**: Resolves method candidates with type arguments (line 135)\n- **PropertyOverloadResolution**: Resolves indexer/property candidates (line 162)\n\nThese methods delegate to the internal **MethodOrPropertyOverloadResolution** (line 183) which is the core resolution engine for both method and property members.\n\n### 2. Generic Type Argument Inference (MethodTypeInference.cs)\nThe **MethodTypeInferrer** struct (defined at line 91) handles C# type inference for generic methods. It provides:\n- **Static Infer method** (line 166): Main entry point for inferring type arguments from method call arguments\n- **InferTypeArgs instance method** (line 555): Performs the two-phase inference process specified in the C# language specification\n\nThe inference process follows the specification with two phases:\n1. First phase: Makes initial inferences of bounds on unfixed type variables\n2. Second phase: Fixes type parameters to specific types and infers further bounds\n\nThis struct maintains extensive state for tracking fixed/unfixed type parameters and their bounds (exact, upper, lower) as specified in the C# spec.\n\n### 3. Method Comparison (OverloadResolution.cs - BetterFunctionMember)\nOnce candidates are deemed applicable, the **BetterFunctionMember** method (lines 1951 and 1990) compares pairs of applicable members. It:\n- Compares conversion sequences for each argument position\n- Uses conversion ranking rules to determine parameter compatibility\n- Returns BetterResult.Left, Right, Neither, or Equal to establish partial ordering\n\nThis method is critical for selecting the single best overload from multiple applicable candidates.\n\n### 4. Conversion Analysis and Ranking (Conversions.cs, ConversionsBase.cs)\nThe **Conversions** class (inheriting from **ConversionsBase**) provides conversion classification:\n- **ClassifyImplicitConversionFromExpression**: Classifies conversions from specific expressions\n- Handles user-defined conversions, standard conversions, and lambda conversions\n- Supports nullable reference type tracking and recursion depth limiting\n\nConversions are used by BetterFunctionMember to rank parameter compatibility and select superior overloads.\n\n### 5. Best Type Inference (BestTypeInferrer.cs)\nThe static **BestTypeInferrer** class handles type inference when no target type is available:\n- **InferBestType** (line 51): Finds best common type for implicitly typed array expressions\n- **InferBestTypeForConditionalOperator** (line 116): Infers type for ternary conditional operator\n- **GetBestType** (line 177): Core algorithm that finds unique best type by pairwise comparison\n\nThis follows section 7.5.2.14 of the C# specification for finding the best common type.\n\n### 6. Supporting Data Structures\n- **AnalyzedArguments** (AnalyzedArguments.cs): Pools analyzed argument expressions, names, and ref kinds\n- **MemberResolutionResult<TMember>** (MemberResolutionResult.cs): Contains resolution outcome for individual members\n- **MemberAnalysisResult** (MemberAnalysisResult.cs): Stores conversion sequences, constraint diagnostics, and argument-to-parameter mappings\n- **OverloadResolution_ArgsToParameters.cs**: Handles complex argument-to-parameter mapping when named arguments, optional parameters, or params modifiers are involved\n\n## The Resolution Chain\n\n1. **MethodInvocationOverloadResolution** receives method candidates, type arguments, receiver, and arguments\n2. For each candidate, **MethodTypeInferrer.Infer** is called to infer missing type arguments\n3. Candidates are filtered by applicability (arguments match parameters)\n4. **BetterFunctionMember** is called repeatedly to find the unique best member\n5. For each parameter position, **Conversions.ClassifyImplicitConversionFromExpression** ranks the conversion quality\n6. If needed, **BestTypeInferrer** infers target types for array/conditional expressions\n7. The winning member is returned in the **OverloadResolutionResult<TMember>**\n\nThis pipeline implements the complete C# 7.x method invocation binding specification, handling generic type inference, overload resolution, and conversion ranking in a coordinated manner."
